                            <div class="player-info-box-header team-giants"><div class="player-info-box-name"><h1>Nick Hundley</h1><div class="player-info-box-name-team"><a href="/teams/giants">San Francisco Giants</a></div></div><div class="player-info-box-item">Age: 34</div><div class="player-info-box-item">Bats/Throws: R/R</div>
        <div class="player-info-box-item">6' 1" / 205</div>
        <div class="player-info-box-pos">C</div></div>
                        <div class="player-info-bio">
                            <strong>Birthdate: </strong>9/8/1983 (34 y, 6 m, 2 d)<br /><b>Drafted:</b> <a href="statss.aspx?playerid=3376&position=C#draft" style="text-decoration:none;">2005 June Amateur Draft - Round: 2, Pick: 28, Overall: 76, Team: San Diego Padres</a><br /><strong>Contract:</strong> <a href="statss.aspx?playerid=3376&position=C#contract" >$2.5M / 1 Years (2018)</a>
                        </div>
                    </td>

(12/19/2017)</div></td></tr>

                    <td>10/19/2015</td><td class="td-badge"><div class="rg badge">RG</div></td><td><a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/is-nick-hundley-sustainable/">Is Nick Hundley Sustainable?</a><span class="m_author"> by <a href="http://www.fangraphs.com/fantasy/index.php?author=64999">Scott Strandberg</a></span></td></tr></table></div></td></tr>

        </td>
        <td style="width: 302px; height: 250px; vertical-align: top;">
            <div class="catchall300" style='width:300px; overflow:hidden;float:right;'><!-- RoS_300x250 --> <div id ='div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13' style='width:300px; height:250px; overflow:hidden;'><script type='text/javascript'>if ($('#div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13').is(':visible')) {googletag.cmd.push(function () { googletag.display('div-gpt-ad-1349421924281-13'); });}</script></div></div>

        </td>
    </tr>
    <tr>
        
        <tr id="so2" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Year in Review: </b>Don't confuse Nick Hundley with Todd Hundley; Nick's offensive contributions pale in comparison to the former Dodger and Met backstop. With that said, the youngster does possess some raw power, as he slammed 20 homers in Double-A in 2007. His ISO rate in the Majors in '09 was a respectable .168 and he could send more homers out of the park as he matures as a hitter. Right now, though, you're getting a player who doesn't hit for average (.238), doesn't drive in many runs (30 in 78 games), and doesn't walk much (9.7%). Oh, and he has a pretty high whiff rate, too.<br /><br /><b>The Year Ahead: </b>Hundley looked to be in line for the lion's share of starts behind the dish in San Diego for 2010, but that may have changed now that the club signed Yorvit Torrealba. The veteran is expected to mentor Hundley, but the latter player could see his playing time reduced if he struggles early. In other words, avoid the young catcher unless he shows enough offensive contributions to earn the regular gig in San Diego. If he starts hitting bombs regularly, which is unlikely given his home ballpark, then you might even want to consider him as a starting catcher in mixed leagues. Just 26, Hundley could show improvements with the bat... just don't count on it.  (Marc Hulet)</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so3" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Throughout his career in the Majors and the minors, Hundley has shown the ability to hit for power and walk at a good clip. However, he also strikes out quite a bit, leading to a low batting average and, thusly, a lower OBP. He dropped his strikeout rate this past season, making contact in and out of the zone at a higher rate. While doing so, he kept up his power numbers, posting a slugging percentage over .400 for the second straight year. Yet, the Padres only felt comfortable playing him in about half of their games, as he started only 73 contests in 2010. Hundley’s value is going to come down to how often the Padres are willing to play him. If he can get 400-plus trips to the plate, expect double-digit home runs and a solid RBI count. His average will hamper his overall value, so he’s not worthy of a draft pick unless you play in a deep or NL-only league. (Zach Sanders)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Hundley has shown good power throughout his career, but he's lacking in most other categories. Unless the Padres commit to using him full-time, there's no need to pay mind to Hundley unless you're in a deep or NL-only league.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so4" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Hundley came on strong for the Friars in 2011, triple-slashing .288/.347/.477 (.354 wOBA) on his way to becoming one of the better every-day bats in San Diego's dismal lineup. Hundley didn't come completely out of nowhere, as his .785 minor league OPS would attest, but it was still a mild surprise on a team that combined to hit .237/.305/.349 and finished worst or second-worst in each triple-slash category in the National League. Petco Park may not be kind to too many hitters, but Hundley found his home park very inviting, to the tune of a .935 OPS and 19 of his 31 extra-base hits on the season. He doesn't have a ton of home run power, but does use his home park to his advantage, with plenty of line drives and ground balls to complement his park's longball-suppressing tendencies. As a result, he has maintained a healthy .165 ISO and should continue to thrive in San Diego. (Brandon Warne)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Among all catchers with 200 or more PA, Hundley was fourth in wOBA, which might surprise you. Be wary of the .362 BABIP, but his batted ball mix should ensure his usefulness to your fantasy squad. In 5x5s he may go a little higher than he's worth, but in saber leagues, he should be a very nice value pick. </td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so5" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>After a strong finish to another injury-plagued season in 2011, expectations were running high for Hundley in 2012. He had shown the ability to hit for above-average power and was respected in the organization enough to warrant a three-year deal with a club option in 2015 in spite of the fact that they had just traded for catching prospect Yasmani Grandal. But Hundley fizzled out again due to another injury and was forced to cut his season short due to August surgery to repair a torn meniscus in his knee. While there was talk of trading the 29-year old backstop once Grandal emerged from Triple-A to take over starting duties, it looks like Hundley will be the Padres starter behind the dish to open 2013 as Grandal was hit with a 50-game suspension for PEDs. If Hundley can stay healthy and produce as he did just prior to his DL stints, then he could be a worthwhile fantasy selection. However, Grandal's suspension ends in late May, so Hundley's future is obviously very dependent on how his potential replacement fares post-punishment. (Howard Bender)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Hundley has shown solid potential both at the plate and behind it, but has failed to produce a full season on the major league level due to injuries throughout his career. Back from elbow surgery in late 2011, he was a beast at the plate, but failed to build on that in 2012 as a torn meniscus in his knee ruined his year. If he can stay healthy, he's worth a look, but with his eventual replacement, Yasmani Grandal, likely due back at the end of May, he is probably playing on borrowed time.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so6" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>With a 50-game suspension levied on expected starting catcher, Yasmani Grandal, Hundley was, again, the Padres' primary backstop in 2013. He opened the year strong with a .329-3-11 batting line through the first month, but faltered soon after and was replaced by a returning Grandal. However a torn ACL for Grandal thrust Hundley back into the starting role and he finished the year with a career best 13 home runs and 44 RBI. But with relatively poor plate discipline (24.0% strikeout and 6.4% walk rate) and a 42.5% ground-ball rate, Hundley's average and on-base percentage remained a detriment to his overall value. He'll carry that mid-level power and career .237 average into 2014 as the primary catcher once again should Grandal not be ready to return, but his overall value remains low as he will only be keeping the seat warm for his contemporary. (Howard Bender)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Hundley was able to hold down the primary catching job in San Diego last year thanks to a suspension and season-ending knee injury to teammate Yasmani Grandal. He posted career numbers, but disappointed the fantasy community with a weak slash line. He'll continue to hold the job in 2014, but for only as long as it takes Grandal to work his way back from his injury.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>The righty-swinging Hundley features reverse platoon splits over nearly 2,000 plate appearances. However, the reason he's suddenly of some interest to fantasy owners is his new home -- Coors Field. Even Michael McKenry was valuable to fantasy teams whilst hitting in Colorado. Hundley will never be an ideal starter in standard fantasy formats, but the occasional spot start at home against a lousy pitcher could be quite beneficial. Keep an eye on Wilin Rosario -- he's the only thing standing between Hundley and 300 plate appearances.(Brad Johnson)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Coors Field brings Hundley back to the fantasy draft board. While he fits best as a streaming option, he could eek out a bigger role if Wilin Rosario is traded.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>The 31-year-old Hundley fits into a unique group of players -- catchers who can hit for batting average. Besides a half dozen or so catchers, most seem to hit .230 with 18 home runs. Hundley doesn’t have the home run potential, but since he gets the extra batting average on balls in play while hitting at Coors, his average is higher than most. High average catchers (Sal Perez is another) can be useful if the rest of your league has drafted low batting average hitters. Additionally, he has the potential for double digit home runs after hitting 13 in 2013 and 10 in 2015. Besides the home runs, he did steal five bases in the 2015, which tied his career high from 2009. I would not expect him to replicate that value again. You may want to platoon Hundley when he's away from home. For playing time, he will be the first-seat catcher in Colorado and have a good 400 plate appearances for the season. Hundley is in play in all but the shallowest of leagues. (Jeff Zimmerman)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Nick Hundley is one of the few catchers with a reasonable batting average. He adds some power and Coors Field as a home field to the traits that make him a decent fantasy option at catcher.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
        <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>On the surface, it would seem like having a catcher who had reached double digits in homers in three of the past four seasons would be a good player to have around. But then you dig a little beneath the surface, and you see that his home run ranks among catchers were t-16th, t-18th and t-21st. In other words, lots of catchers manage to hit 10+ homers each season, so Hundley isn't special in this regard. Hundley managed to cut his strikeout rate and up his isolated power in the past two seasons, but the net result was a 94 wRC+ that ranked just 32nd among catchers. That's not terrible, but when you add that to catching metrics, that left him at the back of the pack by both StatCorner and Baseball Prospectus, and it's not a very encouraging package. Finally, Hundley's CS% has been below league average in two of the past three seasons. The Giants needed someone to back up Buster Posey, and they've tabbed Hundley to do it.  It's hard to kill a serviceable backup catcher, just look at A.J. Pierzynski, but given Hundley's spotty track record, you can't be assured that he will in fact be serviceable. Even if he does land solid playing time, he's not anyone you should be considering for your fantasy squad.<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>There's not much to recommend about Nick Hundley. He isn't really good at hitting, and he isn't really good at catching. That had never really stopped Hundley from getting playing time before, and since Buster Posey can't catch 162 games, it likely won't stop him this year either. </td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
    </tr>
</table>

Hundley managed to cut his strikeout rate and up his isolated power in the past two seasons, but the net result was a 94 wRC+ that ranked just 32nd among catchers. That's not terrible, but when you add that to catching metrics, that left him at the back of the pack by both StatCorner and Baseball Prospectus, and it's not a very encouraging package. Finally, Hundley's CS% has been below league average in two of the past three seasons. The Giants needed someone to back up Buster Posey, and they've tabbed Hundley to do it.  It's hard to kill a serviceable backup catcher, just look at A.J. Pierzynski, but given Hundley's spotty track record, you can't be assured that he will in fact be serviceable. Even if he does land solid playing time, he's not anyone you should be considering for your fantasy squad.",
